# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# Prometheus WAL Write-Ahead Log Segment Management

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in prometheus/prometheus that implement the TSDB write-ahead log (WAL): the WAL segment creation and rotation, the WAL record encoding (series, samples, tombstones), the WAL repair on corrupt segments, and the checkpoint creation to truncate old WAL data.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

88-assistanttext-
I've successfully completed the task and created a comprehensive analysis of the Prometheus TSDB write-ahead log (WAL) implementation. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Overview

The WAL implementation spans **10 core files** in the prometheus/prometheus repository:

### Main WAL Components:
1. **tsdb/wlog/wlog.go** - Core WAL segment management (creation, rotation, writing)
2. **tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go** - Checkpoint creation and truncation
3. **tsdb/wlog/reader.go** - WAL segment reading
4. **tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go** - Live WAL tailing/reading
5. **tsdb/wlog/watcher.go** - WAL record replay and watching
6. **tsdb/record/record.go** - Record types and encoding/decoding

### Supporting Files:
7. **tsdb/head_wal.go** - WAL integration with Head
8. **tsdb/db.go** - Database WAL initialization
9. **tsdb/agent/db.go** - Agent-specific WAL operations
10. **tsdb/repair.go** - WAL repair utilities

## Key Features Documented:

- **Segment Management**: Fixed 128MB segments (configurable) with sequential numbering
- **Record Types**: 10 different record types including Series, Samples, Tombstones, Exemplars, Metadata, and various histogram types
- **Compression**: Snappy/Zstd compression on individual records
- **Encoding**: Delta encoding for timestamps and references, CRC32 validation
- **Checkpoint Creation**: Compacted checkpoints for WAL truncation
- **Repair Mechanism**: Automatic detection and repair of corrupted segments
- **Live Reading**: Support for reading WAL while it's being written

The answer file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details of 50+ symbols and a detailed narrative explanation of the implementation.

\"github.com/prometheus/prometheus\", \"path\": \"tsdb/wlog/wlog.go\", \"symbol\": \"Close\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"# Prometheus TSDB Write-Ahead Log (WAL) Implementation\\n\\nThe Prometheus TSDB WAL consists of a comprehensive set of Go source files in the `github.com/prometheus/prometheus` repository that implement segment-based write-ahead logging for durability and crash recovery.\\n\\n## Core WAL Segment Management (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\n\\nThe main WAL implementation is in `tsdb/wlog/wlog.go`. This file contains the `WL` struct (write log) which manages WAL segments:\\n\\n- **WL struct**: The core WAL manager that handles segment creation, rotation, and record writing. Each segment is a fixed-size file (default 128MB, configurable via `WALSegmentSize` option). Segments are named sequentially as `00000000`, `00000001`, etc.\\n\\n- **Segment creation and rotation**:\\n  - `NewSize()`: Creates a new WAL with specified segment size and compression type. It initializes the first segment and creates an actor-based async worker for efficient writes.\\n  - `New()`: Convenience wrapper for NewSize using the default segment size (128MB).\\n  - `CreateSegment()`: Creates a new segment file in the WAL directory with a specified index.\\n  - `NextSegment()`: Rotates to the next segment asynchronously. This function flushes the current page, creates a new segment, and updates the write pointer.\\n  - `NextSegmentSync()`: Synchronous version of NextSegment for when immediate rotation is needed.\\n  - `SegmentName()`: Builds the filename for a segment given its index.\\n  - `Segments()`: Returns the range [first, last] of existing segments.\\n\\n- **Record writing**: The `Log()` method writes records to the WAL. Records are organized into pages (32KB) within segments. If a record doesn't fit in the current page, the page is flushed and a new page is started. If a record doesn't fit in the current segment, a new segment is automatically created.\\n\\n- **Compression**: WAL supports Snappy and Zstd compression. The compression type is specified during WAL creation and is applied selectively to individual records only if compression saves space.\\n\\n- **Segment information**: `LastSegmentAndOffset()` returns the current segment number and offset within that segment.\\n\\n## WAL Record Encoding (tsdb/record/record.go)\\n\\nThe record package defines the WAL record types and encoding/decoding:\\n\\n- **Record types** (Type enum):\\n  - `Series` (Type=1): Series labels and references\\n  - `Samples` (Type=2): Float sample values\\n  - `Tombstones` (Type=3): Deleted time ranges for series\\n  - `Exemplars` (Type=4): Exemplar data with labels\\n  - `Metadata` (Type=6): Metric metadata (unit, help text)\\n  - `HistogramSamples` (Type=7): Native histogram samples\\n  - `FloatHistogramSamples` (Type=8): Float histogram samples\\n  - `CustomBucketsHistogramSamples` (Type=9): Histograms with custom buckets\\n  - `CustomBucketsFloatHistogramSamples` (Type=10): Float histograms with custom buckets\\n  - `MmapMarkers` (Type=5): Marks for out-of-order samples that have been memory-mapped to disk\\n\\n- **Encoder struct**: Provides methods to encode series, samples, tombstones, exemplars, metadata, and histogram records:\\n  - `Series()`: Encodes series records with their labels\\n  - `Samples()`: Encodes float sample records using delta encoding for timestamps and references\\n  - `Tombstones()`: Encodes deletion markers\\n  - `Exemplars()`: Encodes exemplar data\\n  - `EncodeExemplarsIntoBuffer()`: Low-level exemplar encoding\\n  - `Metadata()`: Encodes metric metadata\\n  - `MmapMarkers()`: Encodes memory-map markers\\n  - `HistogramSamples()`: Encodes native histogram samples\\n  - `FloatHistogramSamples()`: Encodes float histogram samples\\n  - `CustomBucketsHistogramSamples()`: Encodes custom-bucket histograms\\n  - `CustomBucketsFloatHistogramSamples()`: Encodes custom-bucket float histograms\\n\\n- **Decoder struct**: Provides corresponding decode methods to read records:\\n  - `Type()`: Determines the type of a record\\n  - `Series()`: Decodes series records\\n  - `Samples()`: Decodes float samples with delta decompression\\n  - `Tombstones()`: Decodes deletion records\\n  - `Exemplars()`: Decodes exemplar data\\n  - `ExemplarsFromBuffer()`: Low-level exemplar decoding\\n  - `Metadata()`: Decodes metadata records\\n  - `MmapMarkers()`: Decodes memory-map markers\\n  - `HistogramSamples()`: Decodes histogram samples\\n  - `FloatHistogramSamples()`: Decodes float histogram samples\\n  - `DecodeLabels()`: Decodes label pairs\\n  - `DecodeHistogram()`: Decodes histogram structure\\n\\n- **Reference types**: All records reference series by a `HeadSeriesRef` (uint64) which allows efficient series tracking:\\n  - `RefSeries`: Series with labels and reference\\n  - `RefSample`: Float sample with timestamp and value\\n  - `RefMetadata`: Metadata with type, unit, help text\\n  - `RefExemplar`: Exemplar with labels, timestamp, value\\n  - `RefHistogramSample`: Histogram with native histogram structure\\n  - `RefFloatHistogramSample`: Float histogram\\n  - `RefMmapMarker`: Memory-map marker\\n\\n## Checkpoint Creation (tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go)\\n\\nCheckpoints are used to truncate old WAL data and speed up crash recovery:\\n\\n- **Checkpoint() function**: Creates a compacted checkpoint from a range of WAL segments. This function:\\n  - Reads all records from the specified segment range\\n  - Filters out old data (samples below mint timestamp, deleted series, old metadata)\\n  - Creates a new checkpoint directory named `checkpoint.N`\\n  - Stores the checkpoint in segmented format for easy reading\\n  - Returns CheckpointStats with counts of dropped/processed records\\n\\n- **Checkpoint management**:\\n  - `LastCheckpoint()`: Returns the most recent checkpoint directory and index\\n  - `DeleteCheckpoints()`: Deletes checkpoints below a given index\\n  - `DeleteTempCheckpoints()`: Cleans up temporary checkpoint directories from failed checkpoint operations\\n  - `CheckpointStats`: Tracks how many series, samples, tombstones, exemplars, and metadata items were processed and dropped\\n\\n## WAL Reading and Replay (tsdb/wlog/reader.go, tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go)\\n\\n- **Reader struct** (tsdb/wlog/reader.go): Reads completed WAL records from an io.Reader\\n  - `NewReader()`: Creates a new reader\\n  - `Next()`: Advances to the next record and returns true if it exists\\n  - Handles record fragmentation across pages\\n  - Validates CRC32 checksums\\n  - Supports decompression of individual records\\n\\n- **LiveReader struct** (tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go): Reads WAL records from an io.Reader while the WAL is still being written (live tailing)\\n  - `NewLiveReader()`: Creates a live reader with metrics\\n  - Supports reading of incomplete/torn records at EOF\\n  - Exposes `Offset()` to track position in the segment\\n  - Tracks corruption errors via metrics\\n\\n- **OpenReadSegment()**: Opens a specific WAL segment file for reading\\n\\n- **NewSegmentsRangeReader()**: Creates a reader that spans multiple segment ranges, used for reading checkpoints and WAL ranges together\\n\\n## WAL Repair (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\n\\nWhen corruption is detected during WAL replay:\\n\\n- **Repair() method**: Attempts to repair corrupted WAL by:\\n  - Identifying the segment and offset of corruption\\n  - Truncating the corrupted segment to the point before corruption\\n  - Rewriting all records from the checkpoint up to the corruption point\\n  - Deleting all segments after the corrupted one\\n  - Creating a new segment to continue writing\\n\\n- **CorruptionErr struct**: Wraps corruption errors and includes:\\n  - The segment index where corruption occurred\\n  - consists of a comprehensive set of Go source files in the `github.com/prometheus/prometheus` repository that implement segment-based write-ahead logging for durability and crash recovery.\\n\\n## Core WAL Segment Management (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\n\\nThe main WAL implementation is in `tsdb/wlog/wlog.go`. This file contains the `WL` struct (write log) which manages WAL segments:\\n\\n- **WL struct**: The core WAL manager that handles segment creation, rotation, and record writing. Each segment is a fixed-size file (default 128MB, configurable via `WALSegmentSize` option). Segments are named sequentially as `00000000`, `00000001`, etc.\\n\\n- **Segment creation and rotation**:\\n  - `NewSize()`: Creates a new WAL with specified segment size and compression type. It initializes the first segment and creates an actor-based async worker for efficient writes.\\n  - `New()`: Convenience wrapper for NewSize using the default segment size (128MB).\\n  - `CreateSegment()`: Creates a new segment file in the WAL directory with a specified index.\\n  - `NextSegment()`: Rotates to the next segment asynchronously. This function flushes the current page, creates a new segment, and updates the write pointer.\\n  - `NextSegmentSync()`: Synchronous version of NextSegment for when immediate rotation is needed.\\n  - `SegmentName()`: Builds the filename for a segment given its index.\\n  - `Segments()`: Returns the range [first, last] of existing segments.\\n\\n- **Record writing**: The `Log()` method writes records to the WAL. Records are organized into pages (32KB) within segments. If a record doesn't fit in the current page, the page is flushed and a new page is started. If a record doesn't fit in the current segment, a new segment is automatically created.\\n\\n- **Compression**: WAL supports Snappy and Zstd compression. The compression type is specified during WAL creation and is applied selectively to individual records only if compression saves space.\\n\\n- **Segment information**: `LastSegmentAndOffset()` returns the current segment number and offset within that segment.\\n\\n## WAL Record Encoding (tsdb/record/record.go)\\n\\nThe record package defines the WAL record types and encoding/decoding:\\n\\n- **Record types** (Type enum):\\n  - `Series` (Type=1): Series labels and references\\n  - `Samples` (Type=2): Float sample values\\n  - `Tombstones` (Type=3): Deleted time ranges for series\\n  - `Exemplars` (Type=4): Exemplar data with labels\\n  - `Metadata` (Type=6): Metric metadata (unit, help text)\\n  - `HistogramSamples` (Type=7): Native histogram samples\\n  - `FloatHistogramSamples` (Type=8): Float histogram samples\\n  - `CustomBucketsHistogramSamples` (Type=9): Histograms with custom buckets\\n  - `CustomBucketsFloatHistogramSamples` (Type=10): Float histograms with custom buckets\\n  - `MmapMarkers` (Type=5): Marks for out-of-order samples that have been memory-mapped to disk\\n\\n- **Encoder struct**: Provides methods to encode series, samples, tombstones, exemplars, metadata, and histogram records:\\n  - `Series()`: Encodes series records with their labels\\n  - `Samples()`: Encodes float sample records using delta encoding for timestamps and references\\n  - `Tombstones()`: Encodes deletion markers\\n  - `Exemplars()`: Encodes exemplar data\\n  - `EncodeExemplarsIntoBuffer()`: Low-level exemplar encoding\\n  - `Metadata()`: Encodes metric metadata\\n  - `MmapMarkers()`: Encodes memory-map markers\\n  - `HistogramSamples()`: Encodes native histogram samples\\n  - `FloatHistogramSamples()`: Encodes float histogram samples\\n  - `CustomBucketsHistogramSamples()`: Encodes custom-bucket histograms\\n  - `CustomBucketsFloatHistogramSamples()`: Encodes custom-bucket float histograms\\n\\n- **Decoder struct**: Provides corresponding decode methods to read records:\\n  - `Type()`: Determines the type of a record\\n  - `Series()`: Decodes series records\\n  - `Samples()`: Decodes float samples with delta decompression\\n  - `Tombstones()`: Decodes deletion records\\n  - `Exemplars()`: Decodes exemplar data\\n  - `ExemplarsFromBuffer()`: Low-level exemplar decoding\\n  - `Metadata()`: Decodes metadata records\\n  - `MmapMarkers()`: Decodes memory-map markers\\n  - `HistogramSamples()`: Decodes histogram samples\\n  - `FloatHistogramSamples()`: Decodes float histogram samples\\n  - `DecodeLabels()`: Decodes label pairs\\n  - `DecodeHistogram()`: Decodes histogram structure\\n\\n- **Reference types**: All records reference series by a `HeadSeriesRef` (uint64) which allows efficient series tracking:\\n  - `RefSeries`: Series with labels and reference\\n  - `RefSample`: Float sample with timestamp and value\\n  - `RefMetadata`: Metadata with type, unit, help text\\n  - `RefExemplar`: Exemplar with labels, timestamp, value\\n  - `RefHistogramSample`: Histogram with native histogram structure\\n  - `RefFloatHistogramSample`: Float histogram\\n  - `RefMmapMarker`: Memory-map marker\\n\\n## Checkpoint Creation (tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go)\\n\\nCheckpoints are used to truncate old WAL data and speed up crash recovery:\\n\\n- **Checkpoint() function**: Creates a compacted checkpoint from a range of WAL segments. This function:\\n  - Reads all records from the specified segment range\\n  - Filters out old data (samples below mint timestamp, deleted series, old metadata)\\n  - Creates a new checkpoint directory named `checkpoint.N`\\n  - Stores the checkpoint in segmented format for easy reading\\n  - Returns CheckpointStats with counts of dropped/processed records\\n\\n- **Checkpoint management**:\\n  - `LastCheckpoint()`: Returns the most recent checkpoint directory and index\\n  - `DeleteCheckpoints()`: Deletes checkpoints below a given index\\n  - `DeleteTempCheckpoints()`: Cleans up temporary checkpoint directories from failed checkpoint operations\\n  - `CheckpointStats`: Tracks how many series, samples, tombstones, exemplars, and metadata items were processed and dropped\\n\\n## WAL Reading and Replay (tsdb/wlog/reader.go, tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go)\\n\\n- **Reader struct** (tsdb/wlog/reader.go): Reads completed WAL records from an io.Reader\\n  - `NewReader()`: Creates a new reader\\n  - `Next()`: Advances to the next record and returns true if it exists\\n  - Handles record fragmentation across pages\\n  - Validates CRC32 checksums\\n  - Supports decompression of individual records\\n\\n- **LiveReader struct** (tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go): Reads WAL records from an io.Reader while the WAL is still being written (live tailing)\\n  - `NewLiveReader()`: Creates a live reader with metrics\\n  - Supports reading of incomplete/torn records at EOF\\n  - Exposes `Offset()` to track position in the segment\\n  - Tracks corruption errors via metrics\\n\\n- **OpenReadSegment()**: Opens a specific WAL segment file for reading\\n\\n- **NewSegmentsRangeReader()**: Creates a reader that spans multiple segment ranges, used for reading checkpoints and WAL ranges together\\n\\n## WAL Repair (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\n\\nWhen corruption is detected during WAL replay:\\n\\n- **Repair() method**: Attempts to repair corrupted WAL by:\\n  - Identifying the segment and offset of corruption\\n  - Truncating the corrupted segment to the point before corruption\\n  - Rewriting all records from the checkpoint up to the corruption point\\n  - Deleting all segments after the corrupted one\\n  - Creating a new segment to continue writing\\n\\n- **CorruptionErr struct**: Wraps corruption errors and includes:\\n  - The segment index where corruption occurred\\n  - The byte offset within that segment\\n  - The directory containing the corrupted segment\\n\\n## WAL Truncation and Cleanup\\n\\n- **Truncate() method**: Removes all segments before a specified index. Used after checkpointing to clean up old WAL data.\\n- **Sync() method**: Forces an fsync on the current segment (for testing).\\n- **Close() method**: Flushes pending data, pads the current page with zeros, and closes the WAL.\\n\\n## WAL Integration with TSDB\\n\\n- **tsdb/head_wal.go**: Handles WAL replay during Head initialization, includes series, sample, and checkpoint record processing\\n- **tsdb/db.go**: Creates and manages the WAL instance during database initialization\\n- **tsdb/agent/db.go**: Agent-specific WAL truncation based on time windows\\n- **tsdb/repair.go**: Additional repair utilities for index corruption\\n\\n## Key Features\\n\\n1. **Segment-based architecture**: Fixed-size segments prevent individual files from becoming too large and enable efficient truncation\\n2. **Page-based writing**: 32KB pages allow batching of writes and support for compression\\n3. **Record fragmentation**: Large records are split across pages/segments with type markers (full, first, middle, last)\\n4. **Compression support**: Optional Snappy/Zstd compression on individual records\\n5. **CRC32 validation**: Each record includes a CRC32 checksum for corruption detection\\n6. **Delta encoding**: Timestamps and references in samples use delta encoding for space efficiency\\n7. **Asynchronous operations**: Actor-based design for non-blocking segment rotation and fsync\\n8. **Crash recovery**: Automatic repair of corruption detected during replay\\n9. **Checkpoint-based truncation**: Compacted checkpoints enable removal of old WAL segments\\n10. **Concurrent metrics**: Comprehensive Prometheus metrics for monitoring WAL operations\"\n}\n",
